## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and external driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic nonlinearity with damping)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (nonlinear restoring + nonlinear damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → symmetric potential wells
- Even-power terms in x (x²) break spatial symmetry → asymmetric oscillation with different amplitudes in positive/negative directions
- Velocity-position coupling terms like v·x² indicate amplitude-dependent damping, characteristic of self-excited oscillations (van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) indicates external periodic driving forces or parametric excitation
- Cubic restoring force x³ with same sign as linear term x → hardening spring; opposite sign → softening spring with potential escape
- Odd functions of velocity (v, v³) represent dissipative forces; even functions (v²) with sign function represent direction-dependent drag
- Product x·sin(c·t) indicates parametric resonance where the natural frequency is modulated in time
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy considerations (conservative or dissipative) fully determine dynamics
